  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ad9b4fde-7722-45bc-b935-e69fc5268104'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_253068592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253068592" />
    <a title="blackplume" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4735607-blackplume"><img alt="blackplume" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324004731p2/4735607.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253068592?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="blackplume" class="user" itemprop="url" name="blackplume" href="/user/show/4735607-blackplume">blackplume</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253068592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3857060177515133659">Review originally posted in <a href='http://blackplume.wordpress.com/2012/01/16/i-wrote-this-for-you/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blackplume</a><br/><br/><br/>Once in a while you found a book that somehow felt that it is written personally for you. As if the author writes the book with you in his mind, and the dedication has your name written on it. I Wrote This For You is one of those rare books if ever there is already one out there existing. It is also a kind of book that felt like you wrote by yourself for someone you love and care. As if the author write down all the feelings and thoughts you cannot express a</span>
  <span id="freeText3857060177515133659" style="display:none">Review originally posted in <a href="http://blackplume.wordpress.com/2012/01/16/i-wrote-this-for-you/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blackplume</a><br /><br /><br />Once in a while you found a book that somehow felt that it is written personally for you. As if the author writes the book with you in his mind, and the dedication has your name written on it. I Wrote This For You is one of those rare books if ever there is already one out there existing. It is also a kind of book that felt like you wrote by yourself for someone you love and care. As if the author write down all the feelings and thoughts you cannot express and manage to put them on the pages of this lovely book.<br /><br />The book is divided into four parts: Sun, Moon, Stars, and Rain. It includes collections of photos, messages or poems that express real feelings and emotions. Each collections are artistically combined that somehow will touch your soul. The photos alone are carefully pick to show the different angle of life. Each descriptions and messages are heartwarming and inspiring. The photos captures life and the messages express the stories behind it. Stories we can all relate to and messages we all shares. <br /><br />Reading those words somehow felt that the author took the words out of my soul and put it on paper. As if he really knew me so well, like a bestfriend I always wanted to have and he easily put into words all I wanted to say. There are so many quotations from the book that I can relate to, words that triggered memories from the past and give a glimpse of a bright future. It is like peeking into my diary and reading all the words I am silently keeping or letters I never send. It tells my story and everyone’s stories too.<br /><br />There is one particular part of the book that makes me teary because the photo and the message really hit me. It reminds me of one of the place I visit in Taipei though it’s not exactly the same place it reminds me of my stay there. Of all the places I visited so far, Taiwan is the most memorable not only because that’s my first out of the country trip but also because of the experiences it gives me. In my eight days of stay there I experience the ups and down of life. I went through different emotions while I’m there. The experiences and adventures gives me not just memories but also molds me to be a better person. Reminding me those moments somehow resurrect me again to my soul. It reminds me of the people I love and care, people I lost and things that really matters in life.<br /><br />I Wrote This For You is such a short read but the words it delivers expand beyond the pages. The messages are bleak, hopeful, real, and poignant. Add the mysterious and daunting photos, this book is written for you and only you by someone who dares to show how much you matter in this world and reminds you that there is someone who cares and life has meaning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3857060177515133659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13602472779929607498">Even before I saw the ARC of this book, I was already looking for a copy of this in a local bookstore here in the country. But it was always out of stock, hence I never have the chance to check out why there is a lot of good feedback about it. I was so delighted that there's an available reading copy, thus I immediately grab the opportunity to download it.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550587221i/27087918._SY540_.jpg' alt='I Wrote This For You by Iain S.   <span id="freeText13602472779929607498" style="display:none">Even before I saw the ARC of this book, I was already looking for a copy of this in a local bookstore here in the country. But it was always out of stock, hence I never have the chance to check out why there is a lot of good feedback about it. I was so delighted that there's an available reading copy, thus I immediately grab the opportunity to download it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550587221i/27087918._SY540_.jpg" alt="I Wrote This For You by Iain S. Among the four sections, I like the last because I found a lot of good ones in that portion. Several of the poems that are remarkable for me is The Nature of my Body, The Video on the Way Down, The Trees That Decided Not To Die, and The World Needs More Lighthouses.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1550587221i/27087919._SY540_.jpg" alt="I Wrote This For You by Iain S. Thomas" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Overall, there are 21 poems that I think are quite exceptional from this collection; while some of the odes are okay, there are others that are mediocre.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_869193805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/869193805" />
    <a title="Arvy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15194470-arvy"><img alt="Arvy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602998123p2/15194470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/869193805?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arvy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arvy" href="/user/show/15194470-arvy">Arvy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer869193805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8220794607645596631">Congratulations Author! You have just gathered <b>the shattered divine chakras that are confined to heal your <i>own</i> pathetic emotional wounds</b>. I'm so proud of you. Now lock yourself in a room, reread your book eight times and glue your shit together.<br/><br/>This book is a collection of prose and poetry written out of <b>intense heartaches, depressed judgments, schizophrenic thinking and Fly High drugs.</b> At first, I adore how the author contemplates about human emotions - how they revolve around every core of our</span>
  <span id="freeText8220794607645596631" style="display:none">Congratulations Author! You have just gathered <b>the shattered divine chakras that are confined to heal your <i>own</i> pathetic emotional wounds</b>. I'm so proud of you. Now lock yourself in a room, reread your book eight times and glue your shit together.<br /><br />This book is a collection of prose and poetry written out of <b>intense heartaches, depressed judgments, schizophrenic thinking and Fly High drugs.</b> At first, I adore how the author contemplates about human emotions - how they revolve around every core of our atoms, how they trigger earthly and heavenly impulses and the plenty little things that they offer but then, its exaggeration and sugarcoating has flee to Pluto that I no longer know how to fathom them. Some stuff were cliché - lyrics from a song, a segment from a quote, a phrase from a television advertisement. <br /><br />As much as I respect wordcraft, the author turned out bludgeoning its beauty. The writing was a mixture of simple words crafted ambitiously. Yet, it barely pulled through. Here take a read:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Just pretend you’re in a movie. Be as brave and as full of love as the main character. Because we all need to believe in movies, sometimes.”<br /><br />“You were better to the ones that were worse for you. And worse to the one that was better for you.”<br /><br />“You cannot go back in time, even if you wish it with every fiber of your being, your heart and soul, even if you think about it every day.<br />Trust me. I know.”<br /><br />“After darkness, there is always light and you get reminded of this every morning but still you choose to believe that the night will last forever. Nothing lasts forever. Not the good or the bad. So you might as well smile while you’re here."<br /><br />“If you don’t think I’m important “you’re a no one, not a someone. Because everyone is important to someone.”<br /><br />“The bad news is, people are crueler meaner and more evil than you’ve ever imagined. The good news is, people are kinder, gentler and more loving than you’ve ever dreamed.”<br /><br />“That the difference between pain and love is time. That love is only as real as you want it to be. That if you feel good, you look good but it doesn’t always work the other way around.<br />That the sun will rise each day and it’s up to you each day if you match it. That nothing matters up until this point. That what you decide now, in this moment, will change the future. Forever. That rain is beautiful.<br />And so are you.” </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>FUCK YOU, PRICK.</b><br /><br />I recommend this book to jejegirls who are either in love or in need of love or broken or just feeling all the shit the world gladly offers.<br /><br />This would have been good if the author had given importance to the following points:<br /><br />1. <u>
  <b>PHOTOGRAPHS</b>
</u><br />It seems to me that the author is a little less like a thief snagging pictures on Flickr. <i>(Not that I'm certain though. Hihi.)</i> Worse is, what he got out of the box were a bunch of creepy <b>- not creepy cool Ransom Riggs, but creepy creepy unlikely -</b> photographs. The book showed more than one photo of an antediluvian Buddha or who ever it was, effortlessly squinting his eyes <i>(Oh wait. Belated Happy Birthday Buddha, I'm sorry for even including you here)</i> over my imperfect reading posture and I'm like, bullshit, the photos are not working. Artistic proportions and bokehful symmetry were consistent trends among the photos but then along the way, a photo popped showing typical Asian highschoolers in the streets smiling at the camera that you might as well find in a yearbook. CRAAAP. JUST CRAP. How could you put your own selfie in your own graphic book? Hashtag Shameless Sunday. Best solution? Tear off all the photographs.<br /><br />2. <u>
  <b>SEQUENCING</b>
</u><br />The book took off from teenage-i-crush-you-you-crush-them-i'm-invisible feels to eventually <i>you</i> and <i>I</i> falling in love with each other to conflicts and then to a truckload of stupid things which made me conclude that the author went nutts in the end. I think the author wasn't able to chronologically arrange the pieces. One moment it was good. Then it was bad. Then it was good. Then bad. Then crazy. Then good. Then fuck. I felt cheated.<br /><br />2. <b>
  <u>PRONOUNS AND HIMSELF</u>
</b><br />The real problem here is the title. It should have been <i>
  <b>I Wrote This for Me</b>
</i>. Really. The progression of pronouns from you to I probably went off unnoticed by the author since he was confused by who were who. Truth be told, the author himself was both <i>you</i> and <i>I</i>. <b>Amazing uncovering. Damn. Father Palahniuk, I did it.</b> Okay. Kidding aside, I think <i>you</i> are somewhere between narcissistic and problematic. However, the book is there to help you.<br /><br />Author. Whoever you are. I wrote this review for <i>you</i>. Yes, you. <b>No shit.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8220794607645596631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1060842503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1060842503" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1060842503?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060842503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13278584214393322409">Having had some time to think about this, I feel like this style of poems/quotes works better and has greater impact when each is viewed alone. If you read one quoted somewhere online, then it can seem quite deep and profound and steeped in beautiful truth. But when you sit and read through pages and pages of the same, it feels cheesy and contrived. At least, it does to me.<br/><br/>Imagine you're on a date and the other person says you're beautiful (or the equivalent). At first, that seems really nice an</span>
  <span id="freeText13278584214393322409" style="display:none">Having had some time to think about this, I feel like this style of poems/quotes works better and has greater impact when each is viewed alone. If you read one quoted somewhere online, then it can seem quite deep and profound and steeped in beautiful truth. But when you sit and read through pages and pages of the same, it feels cheesy and contrived. At least, it does to me.<br /><br />Imagine you're on a date and the other person says you're beautiful (or the equivalent). At first, that seems really nice and you probably get all warm and tingly inside. But if they don't stop, if they continue on and on by saying: "You are the most beautiful person I have ever seen. Your eyes are like the deepest ocean. Your hair is like liquid chocolate." I mean, pass me the bucket. Also, I no longer believe a single word they say. <br /><br />That's kinda how these books of poetry make me feel.<br /><br />I would have liked this much more during my teenage emo phase. Nowadays, it seems cliche and extremely emotionally manipulative. And emotionally manipulative books are those that leave me feeling most emotionless of all. It's slightly better written, but I would recommend this for fans of the modern tumblr quote-style poetry - think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7012565.Lang_Leav" title="Lang Leav" rel="nofollow noopener">Lang Leav</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8075577.Rupi_Kaur" title="Rupi Kaur" rel="nofollow noopener">Rupi Kaur</a> and/or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15225448.Amanda_Lovelace" title="Amanda Lovelace" rel="nofollow noopener">Amanda Lovelace</a>.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_1150900060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1150900060" />
    <a title="Es Summer " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15104379-es-summer"><img alt="Es Summer " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466450844p2/15104379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1150900060?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Es Summer " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Es Summer " href="/user/show/15104379-es-summer">Es Summer </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15104379-es-summer?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15104379-es-summer?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1150900060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer672248613827567624">This book is mine.<br/>It's written with me in its mind. <br/>All these words are for me. <br/>Only for me.<br/>The title even says it: I Wrote This For You.<br/>And it is.<br/>This little piece of magic touches me so deeply that I want to dig my fingers in its papers and hold it tight, forever.<br/><br/>This book shares my secrets with you guys.<br/>My feelings, hard to formulate in words, but this author does that exactly.<br/>It feels like a warm hug, a soft smile and a comforting word all in a dreamy book about ME. <br/>But it was like that for </span>
  <span id="freeText672248613827567624" style="display:none">This book is mine.<br />It's written with me in its mind. <br />All these words are for me. <br />Only for me.<br />The title even says it: I Wrote This For You.<br />And it is.<br />This little piece of magic touches me so deeply that I want to dig my fingers in its papers and hold it tight, forever.<br /><br />This book shares my secrets with you guys.<br />My feelings, hard to formulate in words, but this author does that exactly.<br />It feels like a warm hug, a soft smile and a comforting word all in a dreamy book about ME. <br />But it was like that for you as well, right?<br /><br /><b>
  <i> "The world will carry on without you and me when we're gone.<br />Let it carry on."<br /><br />"The heart we share.<br />Every time,<br />they cut you,<br />I bleed."<br /><br /></i>
</b>It's not often you come across a book that speaks directly to your soul.<br />It's not often that you wish you could call the author of a book you just finished to talk about life with said author.<br />It's not often that your whole book is highlighted, because almost every poem felt like yours. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I know you're not here, <br />I can see it in your eyes when we talk.<br />Where ever you are,<br />Come back soon."<br /><br />"You were better to the ones that were worse for you.<br />And worse to the one that was better for you."<br /><br /></i>
</b> I Wrote This For You is a little bit magic and words. It's a simple idea. The book is filled with poems and photo's. The photo's are simple.<br />Photo's of our daily lives, but the way it is presented, with the poems, makes is something more. A subway is suddenly loneliness, the trees become love, the ocean is kindness and your mind is the creator of the story. This book is YOURS. The words are chosen thoughtfully. The author is speaking directly to you and everyone will see something else in it. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"And you will find no fear here,<br />in unkind words,<br />or the hardness of others.<br />And you fill find no sadness here,<br />in the meanness of the world,<br />in the anger that comes from those who feel small,<br />And you will find no hurt here, <br />in a million insults or a single, softly spoken lie.<br />Because only a hard heart shatters.<br />Only a hard heart breaks."<br /><br />"You're okay.<br />Breathe. Just breathe.<br />Open your eyes. Come back.<br />It's over now. You're okay. Wake up. Please wake up. Don't do this to me.<br />Don't do this to me. I love you so fucking much. Come back."<br /><br />"Don't you dare to tell me nothing matters.<br />Everything matters.<br />Every fucking drop of rain, every ray of sunlight, every wisp of cloud matters and they matter because I can see them, and if I can see them, they can see me. I know that there's an entire world that cares out there, hiding behind a world that doesn't, afraid to show who it really is and with or without you, I will drag that world out of the dirt and the blood until we live in it.<br />Until we all live in it."<br /><br /></i>
</b> Overall, a great poetic read about life, love, the nature and loneliness.<br />I Wrote This For You is indeed written for you. Just for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="672248613827567624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_523089618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/523089618" />
    <a title="Erin Hobbs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9569217-erin-hobbs"><img alt="Erin Hobbs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396304948p2/9569217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/523089618?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin Hobbs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin Hobbs" href="/user/show/9569217-erin-hobbs">Erin Hobbs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer523089618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9109286503134585452">This book is extremely special. "I Wrote This For You" is exactly what it sounds like; a book written for you. There are two subjects throughout this whole book- "you" and "me". This allows the reader to apply the short stories to anyone or anything they want. It could be a boyfriend, a girlfriend, a mom, dad or sibling. Granted some of the stories may be more aplicable to a significant other/ lover versus a sibling, but there is still the ability of choice due to no names. Although a majority o</span>
  <span id="freeText9109286503134585452" style="display:none">This book is extremely special. "I Wrote This For You" is exactly what it sounds like; a book written for you. There are two subjects throughout this whole book- "you" and "me". This allows the reader to apply the short stories to anyone or anything they want. It could be a boyfriend, a girlfriend, a mom, dad or sibling. Granted some of the stories may be more aplicable to a significant other/ lover versus a sibling, but there is still the ability of choice due to no names. Although a majority of these stories are short, sometimes only a sentence, they carry the shadow of longer days.<br /><br />The fact that with one sentence you can imagine a whole person, is one of my favorite parts about the book. I love that the reader is able to apply that sentence to anyone that they may know, or completely make up the background of the story. I really enjoy envisioning the lives of two people who go to the circus all the time, or hopscotch through a mall. Its fun to imagine the author (Iain Thomas) writing these stories; who was he writing about??<br /><br />The other thing that I really enjoy about this book is the fact that it is a collaboration piece. Iain Thomas is a South African writer (that's what initially drew me to him) who collaborated with his friend, whom he met online, who was a photographer living in Japan. The pictures add to the stories significantly. The visual representation of a scene or place to associate with these stories allows for greater understanding. <br /><br />I will most likely be passing this book around to my friends if I can bear to part with it for a little while. The stories are entrancing and I think anyone would enjoy it. The whole concept is neat, and I feel that everyone should experience reading a book that was 'written for them'. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9109286503134585452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16027370227934769512">I’ve decided I need to stop reading “trendy poetry”... This was good, but it was just good. I like poetry that makes me cry or makes me say “wow” or makes me feel understood. This book was nice at times & I dog-eared a few pages, but I truly only thought maybe 10 out of the 194 pages were decent. It was a breeze through read & I just don’t understand why so many people obsessed over it. It has won awards, gotten outstanding recommendations here on goodreads... but I just don’t get it. Maybe I am</span>
  <span id="freeText16027370227934769512" style="display:none">I’ve decided I need to stop reading “trendy poetry”... This was good, but it was just good. I like poetry that makes me cry or makes me say “wow” or makes me feel understood. This book was nice at times &amp; I dog-eared a few pages, but I truly only thought maybe 10 out of the 194 pages were decent. It was a breeze through read &amp; I just don’t understand why so many people obsessed over it. It has won awards, gotten outstanding recommendations here on goodreads... but I just don’t get it. Maybe I am alone in this. Or maybe I’m being pessimistic.... But to me this was a collection of heartbreak &amp; longing that should’ve just been posted on tumblr. I’m sorry if you loved this book &amp; my review offends you, but I’m just looking to understand the hype. Comment if you’ve read this &amp; what you thought. I feel as if I’m being a bit of a harsh critic... Lol. Just particular about my poetry. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1642732366" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1642732366?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henz" href="/user/show/19767615-henz">Henz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642732366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14630321972386446089"><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>
      "I need you to understand something. I wrote this for you. I wrote this for you and only you. Everyone else who reads it, doesn’t get it. They may think they get it, but they don’t. This is the sign you’ve been looking for. You were meant to read these words."
    </em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book is a collection of of poetry and photograph written for you. Not everybody will be able to understand this book. I like this kind of style to combine photography and literature because I also use it on <a href='https://thebookwormpanda.wordpress.com/the-poet-in-me-or-what-i-assume-to-be/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <strong>
</strong></a></span>
  <span id="freeText14630321972386446089" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>
      "I need you to understand something. I wrote this for you. I wrote this for you and only you. Everyone else who reads it, doesn’t get it. They may think they get it, but they don’t. This is the sign you’ve been looking for. You were meant to read these words."
    </em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br /><br />This book is a collection of of poetry and photograph written for you. Not everybody will be able to understand this book. I like this kind of style to combine photography and literature because I also use it on <a href="https://thebookwormpanda.wordpress.com/the-poet-in-me-or-what-i-assume-to-be/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <strong>
    <em>my poems</em>
  </strong>
</a> except the pictures are borrowed. LOL^^ Thank Google for that.<br /><br />This book comes with honest feelings about adoration, hurt and moving on. If you are <em>cynic</em> then this is not for you because you'll just find that the prose and poetry came from a depressed person but I dig this kind of thing; it doesn't need to rhyme, just pure honest feelings. Because that's what poetry and art is, it's about expression.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>"So yes, we could kiss. I could kiss you and you could kiss me. There’s no science, plane ticket or clock stopping us. But if we kiss, it will end the world. And I’ve ended the world before. No one survived. Least of all me."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br />I'm just not fan of the photographs. I mean who am I to question photography because I have little knowledge of it. In my opinion some of the photographs matches the poetry and prose, some just don't. Again this poetry book is not for all, but compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18003300-love-misadventure?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Lang Leav's Love and Misadventure </a>I rather like this one.<br /><br />I recommend this to people who embrace melancholy and to those who have a lot of feelings. LOL^^</span>

<div id="review_663254054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/663254054" />
    <a title="Alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7236277-alexandra"><img alt="Alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483304704p2/7236277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/663254054?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra" href="/user/show/7236277-alexandra">Alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer663254054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3053978740818648930">I really hoped to like this, because the few bits and pieces that I saw floating around were really great aphorisms. But the thing as a whole was just so much of the same, and it felt like the punch line to every single piece was 'for YOU'; I mean, even the title follows that formula. That's not necessarily a bad thing in itself, but it gets old after a while. So many cliches, one after another, all to render the same stereotypical responses... it just had this overly dramatic teenage-angst feel</span>
  <span id="freeText3053978740818648930" style="display:none">I really hoped to like this, because the few bits and pieces that I saw floating around were really great aphorisms. But the thing as a whole was just so much of the same, and it felt like the punch line to every single piece was 'for YOU'; I mean, even the title follows that formula. That's not necessarily a bad thing in itself, but it gets old after a while. So many cliches, one after another, all to render the same stereotypical responses... it just had this overly dramatic teenage-angst feel going on that I couldn't stomach. The author wrote some nice snippets that stood alright on their own, but for a collection, I felt like this constant reversal back to the eponymous 'you' and the plodding, redundant themes made it far too formulaic and contrived to actually enjoy.<br /><br />That said, I can see why other people enjoyed it so much, and all the more power to them. Me, I just want a refund.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3053978740818648930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2024119780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1710883360300805474"><i>
  <b>“And everyone, somewhere, is someone, if we only give them a chance.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>I have no words. Really. This felt as if i were reading someone's personal, precious words, not a book. I related to so many of those words on different levels, and i couldn't help but savour each single one of them. <br/><br/>It was very enjoyable, and unlike any poetry book that i've read before. I read it carefully, for some reason, as if the words will fade if i read them too quickly. The photographs are mesmerising, and sometime</span>
  <span id="freeText1710883360300805474" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“And everyone, somewhere, is someone, if we only give them a chance.”</b>
</i><br /><br />I have no words. Really. This felt as if i were reading someone's personal, precious words, not a book. I related to so many of those words on different levels, and i couldn't help but savour each single one of them. <br /><br />It was very enjoyable, and unlike any poetry book that i've read before. I read it carefully, for some reason, as if the words will fade if i read them too quickly. The photographs are mesmerising, and sometimes i'd catch myself staring at a few of them for a minute or two. I have no enough words for this, but it's more than fair to say that i loved it.</span>

<div id="review_830250010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/830250010" />
    <a title="Hannah (bookwormstalk)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12190532-hannah-bookwormstalk"><img alt="Hannah (bookwormstalk)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597548888p2/12190532.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17420067492288085559">The type of poetry: <i>
  <b>Free Verse</b>
</i> <br/><i>How many hearts would have be invaded for the every reasons, if each time you said “I love you”, you meant it?</i> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514383849ra/24768518.gif' width='500' height='269' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>Take a hint! How about the hierarchical order of you, two people, people, and the whole world together? This one flows in that order. Rather than stating it as poetry, I would say that these are quotations emphasized on love, life, surviving obstacles, leading optimism and much more. The beautiful familiar snippets put together with the evocative appr</span>
  <span id="freeText17420067492288085559" style="display:none">The type of poetry: <i>
  <b>Free Verse</b>
</i> <br><i>How many hearts would have be invaded for the every reasons, if each time you said “I love you”, you meant it?</i> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514383849ra/24768518.gif" width="500" height="269" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Take a hint! How about the hierarchical order of you, two people, people, and the whole world together? This one flows in that order. Rather than stating it as poetry, I would say that these are quotations emphasized on love, life, surviving obstacles, leading optimism and much more. The beautiful familiar snippets put together with the evocative approach. Some of them do hold layered connotation and some are too simplistic. I admire the <b>Title</b> + <b>Photograph</b> + <b>Canto</b> concept. Some of them do lack depth but it glorifies as we usually neglect the on-going small things around us. <br><i>Of course it’s complicated. If it wasn’t, I probably wouldn’t be interested in you.</i> <br>The archetypal which addresses <b>“YOU”</b> in a direct manner, it sings faintly starting from personal problems to the world.<br><i>Just like you mistook lust for love, you have mistaken being alone with loneliness. So I’m fine. Thank you for asking.</i><br>P.S.: I cannot state drawbacks of any poetry because it is coated with unknown layers so this one is for everyone who acknowledges the emotion - <b>“LOVE”</b>. This one will console you - "You are not alone!" <br><i>You are a drop of perfect in an imperfect world. And all I need is a taste.</i> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514385520ra/24768813.gif" width="500" height="284" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_433245503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/433245503" />
    <a title="Yoonji" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13264515-yoonji"><img alt="Yoonji" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527565356p2/13264515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/433245503?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yoonji" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yoonji" href="/user/show/13264515-yoonji">Yoonji</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer433245503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12029478538505790737"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.theinkgobbler.blogspot.com/'>http://www.theinkgobbler.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>I'm sure every single person on this planet has had moments in his or her life where things just don't work out the way they want them to. Maybe you're hungry but there's no more milk left to suck out of the bottle. Maybe you got caught in a sudden downpour and your socks are squelching and gross. Maybe you just broke up with someone you really love. Maybe you got fired from work and now you don't know what to do. These are the moments when you feel hurt or </span>
  <span id="freeText12029478538505790737" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theinkgobbler.blogspot.com/">http://www.theinkgobbler.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br />I'm sure every single person on this planet has had moments in his or her life where things just don't work out the way they want them to. Maybe you're hungry but there's no more milk left to suck out of the bottle. Maybe you got caught in a sudden downpour and your socks are squelching and gross. Maybe you just broke up with someone you really love. Maybe you got fired from work and now you don't know what to do. These are the moments when you feel hurt or angry or listless or sad. But sometimes, there are little things that end up brightening your day, even if its by the smallest of degrees. This book is one of those little things.<br /><br />"I Wrote This For You" is a collection of nearly 200 of the most beautiful and meaningful entries about life, love, loss, beginnings, ending, and, above all, hope. Each of the four distinct chapters--Sun, Moon, Stars, Rain--explores the different facets of these themes of our lives and, in the process, brings readers to an understanding of themselves.<br /><br />The photographs, the chapter titles, and the entries themselves all work together beautifully to really tug at your heart strings. What struck me was how personal each and every entry was. Being a hopeless romantic myself, I could relate to or at least imagine the emotions and images behind the simply-worded sentences. I can't help but to connect my own personal experiences to what's written on the page--which is precisely what the author had intended. Here's one of my favourite entries:<br /><br />I don't know if you felt that or not. <br />But it felt like two people kissing after hours of thinking about it. <br />It felt like two people talking after nights of silence. <br />It felt like two people touching after weeks of being numb. <br />It felt like two people facing each other after months of looking away.<br />It felt like two people in love after years of being alone. <br />And it felt like two people meeting each other, after an entire lifetime of not meeting each other.<br /><br />It's so beautiful. The emotions wrought in the words really call out to you, almost to the point where they're palpable. You feel the relief, the breathtaking moment when you finally do that something or meet that someone. You become both the 'me' and the 'you'. There's a sweet sadness behind it, but, at the same time, there's hope, too. The simplicity of the language really reminds me that life is just that--it's not some grand movie or drama on a stage. Instead, life is life and nothing more. We smile, laugh, cry, yell, have good moments and bad moments, and, in the end, it comes down to us living through each and every day.<br /><br />This short, sweet book is really a story of your own life. It really touches something inside of you, and I even went on the blog that the entries were originally from to read more. The words linger, and that's truly the most important gift a book can ever give you. I highly recommend picking up a copy--it will stay with you for days, if not years.<br /><br />Rating: 5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="12029478538505790737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Farhana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52763346-farhana"><img alt="Farhana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561916657p2/52763346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1970324278?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Farhana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Farhana" href="/user/show/52763346-farhana">Farhana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52763346-farhana?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970324278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18337130941778754080">"Oh shut up. Every time it rains, it stops raining. Every time you hurt, you heal. After darkness, there is always light and you get reminded of this every morning but still you choose to believe that the night will last forever. Nothing lasts forever. Not the good or the bad. So you might as well smile while you’re here." <br/><br/>A School for Fools আর Dear Friend, From My Life I Write to You in Your Life এর পর আরেকটা বই যেটা অবশ্যই আমার পছন্দের তালিকায় থাকবে ।<br/><br/>ব্রেক আপ শব্দটা এত কমন আর রেগুলার হয়ে গেছ</span>
  <span id="freeText18337130941778754080" style="display:none">"Oh shut up. Every time it rains, it stops raining. Every time you hurt, you heal. After darkness, there is always light and you get reminded of this every morning but still you choose to believe that the night will last forever. Nothing lasts forever. Not the good or the bad. So you might as well smile while you’re here." <br /><br />A School for Fools আর Dear Friend, From My Life I Write to You in Your Life এর পর আরেকটা বই যেটা অবশ্যই আমার পছন্দের তালিকায় থাকবে ।<br /><br />ব্রেক আপ শব্দটা এত কমন আর রেগুলার হয়ে গেছে যে আমি এই শব্দটা ব্যবহার করব না ।<br />যখন ভালোবাসার মানুষ দূরে চলে যায় , তারপরে যে মানুষটা পড়ে রইল তার প্রতি মুহূর্তের অনুভবের বিবরণ, অনুভূতির বিবর্তন পাওয়া যাবে এই লেখায়।<br />অসহ্য স্মৃতিকাতড়তার যন্ত্রণা, একাকীত্ব, অসহায়ত্ব, ক্ষোভ, রাগ, কষ্ট , জিজ্ঞাসা , ভেঙ্গে যাওয়া স্বপ্নের টুকরো হাতে করে উদ্দেশ্যহীনতায় বসে থাকা , যা কিছু জীবনের একটা বড় অংশ জুড়ে পরিব্যাপ্ত ছিল তার হঠাত না থাকার শূন্যতা । অনেক অবোধ , সান্ত্বনা না মানা প্রশ্ন কোন উত্তরে যার পরিতৃপ্তি হয় না । <br />হয়ত আবার সব ঠিক হবে তার অপেক্ষা... <br />পুরোনো নিজেকে যে ভালো থাকত তাকে প্রচণ্ড মিস করা, আবার সেই পুরোনো আমি তে ফিরে যাবার, ভালো থাকার তীব্র পিপাসা। ভালো থাকা কে ধরে রাখতে যা ক্রমাগত মন কে আহত করছে তাকে অস্বীকারের সাময়িক চেষ্টা ।<br /><br />তবু মানুষকে একসময় সবকিছু কাটিয়ে উঠতে হয় নিজের বাঁচার জন্যে, ভালোভাবে বাঁচার জন্যে ...<br /> <br />Daughter এর Medicine গানের কথায় ,<br />You could still be,<br />what you want to.<br />What you said you were,<br />when I met you.<br />when you met me.<br />when I met you.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer492787902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14475290231525531608">I Wrote This For You is wonderful because it can speak to so many people at so many different levels. For myself, the quotation, “You forget that, in the dark, we must move closer together in order to see each other. You were never alone.” which is featured in the book, spoke to me. When I read this passage, I immediately thought of myself as a adolescent battling depression as well as my family and friends who are currently battling depression. With depression, it is so difficult to see the lig</span>
  <span id="freeText14475290231525531608" style="display:none">I Wrote This For You is wonderful because it can speak to so many people at so many different levels. For myself, the quotation, “You forget that, in the dark, we must move closer together in order to see each other. You were never alone.” which is featured in the book, spoke to me. When I read this passage, I immediately thought of myself as a adolescent battling depression as well as my family and friends who are currently battling depression. With depression, it is so difficult to see the light. Even when good things happen, one still feels lost. What makes this quote understandable, to me, is that it shows you that you are not alone even when things seem to be that way. With that said, this passage can be interpreted a number of different ways for a number of different people.<br /><br />The book has a certain versatility that is remarkable. If this book, as well as the passages, are as popular as they've become then it says one thing about humans - we are much more similar than we believe. We have gone through similar heartbreaks, love affairs, hardships, and experiences. Maybe we just need to communicate more often (or share favorite passages in this book!) to understand our similarities rather than focusing on our differences.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14475290231525531608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1675320715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11626464633916797484">" There are a million ways to bleed but you are by far my favorite . "<br/>This was beautiful , like how adorable are these titles and these little poems and photographs and how they all come together in such harmony. <br/>Night trains , broken lights , tunnels ,Buddha , beer , weak hands and coldness felt like pictures from a far dream , fleeting visions of love and hurt and half-lighted candles.<br/> It was such a simple beautiful artistic exprience , connecting these deeply expressed emotions with these vie</span>
  <span id="freeText11626464633916797484" style="display:none">" There are a million ways to bleed but you are by far my favorite . "<br />This was beautiful , like how adorable are these titles and these little poems and photographs and how they all come together in such harmony. <br />Night trains , broken lights , tunnels ,Buddha , beer , weak hands and coldness felt like pictures from a far dream , fleeting visions of love and hurt and half-lighted candles.<br /> It was such a simple beautiful artistic exprience , connecting these deeply expressed emotions with these views and drown in feelings and places . <br />It's like a love song that carries all the feelings . Because love is not always sweet and fun .It can be so painful like that . It can be so beautiful like that .<br />I want to share so many quotes but there's much beauty everywhere that I can't choose .So I just randomly picked this one about lost chances with a fine feeling of reincarnation : <br />"Joan of Arc came back as a little girl in Japan, and her father told her to stop listening to her imaginary friends.<br />Elvis was born again in a small village in Sudan, he died hungry, age 9, never knowing what a guitar was.<br />Michelangelo was drafted into the military at age 18 in Korea, he painted his face black with shoe polish and learned to kill.<br />Jackson Pollock got told to stop making a mess, somewhere in Russia.<br />Hemingway, to this day, writes DVD instruction manuals somewhere in China. He's an old man on a factory line. You wouldn't recognize him.<br />Gandhi was born to a wealthy stockbroker in New York. He never forgave the world after his father threw himself from his office window, on the 21st floor.<br />And everyone, somewhere, is someone, if we only give them a chance."</span>
  <a data-text-id="11626464633916797484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N90QtAHEH5bWqDlaRN1f4mIqfHewvkWm0u4kvSWhVmpNbbrE2qJkXE+k/nn9+mW4iPhc6llDnpTL7ryNa45D4Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mt5VHW62wuFKPHNUFWIFtP7gsFCbnwT8UcJA4FH7ByDgbv9ttdC5K9MwtHesRT/uFDKQzXJi385IwtjQH9QSqw==')})
  }

There is no Table of Contents. Instead, there is a &quot;Track List,&quot; making it easy to refer to them to your friends with a, &quot;Hey did you read track seven?!&quot; There are no chapters. Instead, the book is divided into two parts, or as one would say in the 90\'s, two &quot;sides.&quot; Side A holds poetry that touches on all aspects of the human condition like life, death, love, moving on, evolving, growing up, hometowns, family dynamic, life after trauma, and make-ups and breakups. Side B holds the &quot;remixes&quot; of these poems, in the form of blackout poetry, also known as &quot;found poetry.&quot; Side B gives the material a fresh twist by creating new poetry out of Side A. There is also a very special surprise at the end of each track. \n\nAlicia decided to self publish this effort after leaving her publishing house. She views this book as her &quot;independence&quot; and official separation from that venture. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2960173915280948070">pleasefindthis (the pen name of Iain S. Thomas) is best known for the I Wrote This For You project, which he began in 2007 as a blog with photographer, Jon Ellis. The project was published as a book in December of 2011 and appears on bestseller lists weekly. <br/><br/>He lives in Cape Town, South Africa and shares his home with his wife, daughter and various animals. </span>

</div>
